## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: population ecology / mathematical biology (population dynamics ODEs)
**Analysis**: The target dP_dt is the time-derivative of population size P, indicating an ordinary differential equation for population dynamics. With only (t, P) available, the most common structures express density dependence (functions of P) and environmental/seasonal forcing (functions of t) acting on per-capita growth.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Exponential (Malthusian) growth: dP_dt = c0 * P (density-independent per-capita growth)
- Time-varying exponential growth: dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * t) * P (secular trend in per-capita growth due to environment)
- Logistic growth (Verhulst ODE): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) (carrying capacity via quadratic density dependence)
- General polynomial density dependence: dP_dt = P * (c0 + c1 * P + c2 * P**2) (flexible per-capita rate as polynomial in P)
- Theta-logistic: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) (tunable approach to carrying capacity/competition nonlinearity)
- Gompertz growth (ODE form): dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / P) (decelerating growth with log-density dependence)
- Richards growth (ODE form): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2)**c3 (family covering multiple sigmoidal shapes)
- Allee effect (strong Allee, cubic): dP_dt = c0 * P * (c1 * P - 1) * (1 - c2 * P) (negative growth at low P plus carrying capacity at high P)
- Allee effect (rational per-capita): dP_dt = c0 * P * ((P - c1) / (P + c2)) * (1 - c3 * P) (smooth low-density suppression with high-density limitation)
- Constant-yield harvesting: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 (removal independent of population size)
- Proportional harvesting: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 * P (removal proportional to population)
- Seasonally forced growth: dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * sin(c2 * t + c3)) * P * (1 - c4 * P) (periodic environment modulating growth rate)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Density-independent regime: dP_dt proportional to P (straight line through origin when plotting dP_dt vs P at fixed t)
- Carrying capacity/competition: negative quadratic (or higher) term in P so dP_dt crosses zero at a positive P and becomes negative above it
- Per-capita growth diagnosis: writing dP_dt = P * g(P,t) indicates g is the per-capita rate; linear g(P) implies logistic-type dynamics
- Gompertz-type slowing: presence of log(c * P) or log(c / P) implies per-capita growth decreases approximately linearly with log-population
- Allee threshold: factors like (c * P - 1) or (P - c) create a positive equilibrium threshold below which growth is negative
- Harvesting signatures: additive negative constant term implies constant-yield harvest; an extra -c*P term implies proportional harvest/mortality
- Seasonal forcing: sinusoidal terms in t indicate periodic modulation; interaction with P (multiplying P or P*(1-cP)) implies environment changes per-capita growth
- Nonlinear approach to K: exponents on P inside (1 - (c*P)**theta) tune how sharply growth collapses near carrying capacity

GT Equivalence Verification (BPG23)
============================================================
GT: c0*(c1 - P/c2)*P + c3*(c4 - exp(-c5*P))*P
Candidate formulas: 58

Let \(P\) be the only effective variable in the GT (GT does not depend on \(t\)). Rewrite the GT into a canonical form:

\[
\text{GT}(P)=0.5980421690791728\,(1-\tfrac{P}{32.93940240233941})P \;+\;0.5980421690791728\,(1-e^{-0.07682777495563793 P})P
\]

Expand/simplify:

- First term: \(0.5980\,(P - P^2/32.9394)= (0.5980)P - (0.5980/32.9394)P^2\).
- Second term: \(0.5980\,(P - P e^{-kP}) = (0.5980)P - 0.5980\,P e^{-kP}\), where \(k=0.07682777495563793\).

So
\[
\text{GT}(P)= A\,P^2 + B\,P + C\,P e^{-kP}
\]
with
- \(A= -0.5980421690791728/32.93940240233941 \neq 0\) (negative),
- \(B= 2\cdot 0.5980421690791728 \neq 0\),
- \(C= -0.5980421690791728 \neq 0\),
- and crucially the exponential factor is \(e^{-kP}\) multiplied by \(P\) (not a pure exponential term, and not \(e^{+kP}\)).

Therefore any matching candidate must be able to represent **simultaneously**:
1) a nonzero \(P^2\) polynomial term,  
2) a nonzero linear \(P\) term,  
3) a nonzero \(P\cdot e^{-kP}\) term,  
and **no other functional forms** (no logs, sines, rational-in-\(P\) denominators, extra exponentials with different structure, constants, \(t\)-dependence, etc.).

Now check candidates.

---

### 1
Has rational terms \(\frac{P^3}{P+c_1},\frac{P^2}{P+c_1},\frac{1}{P+c_1}\) and pure exponentials \(e^{cP}\) not multiplied by \(P\). Cannot equal \(P e^{-kP}\) for all \(P\) without introducing non-polynomial rational artifacts. **No.**

### 2
Contains \(P^2\) and linear \(P\) terms, but exponential term is \(P\cdot c_3 e^{c_4 P}\) (good shape) **however** also has \(P^{c_5}c_6\) and constant \(c_7\). You can set \(c_6=0\) and \(c_7=0\). Then it becomes
\[
P^2 c_0 + P(c_1+c_2) + P c_3 e^{c_4 P}.
\]
This matches GT form if we choose:
- \(c_0 = A\),
- \(c_1+c_2 = B\),
- \(c_3 = C\),
- \(c_4 = -k\).
All are allowed real constants. **Yes, can match.**

### 3
Has \(P^2 c_0\), \(P c_1\), and \(P c_2 e^{c_3 P}\) (good), but also \(P^{c_4}c_5\) and constant \(c_6\). Set \(c_5=0\) and \(c_6=0\). Then same matching as #2 with \(c_1=B\), \(c_2=C\), \(c_3=-k\), \(c_0=A\). **Yes.**

### 4
Includes a \(\log(Pc_5+1)\) term. GT has no log; cannot cancel a log with polynomial/exponential terms for all \(P\). **No.**

### 5
Includes \(\log(Pc_6+1)\). Same issue. **No.**

### 6
Has \(P^2 c_0 + P c_1 + P c_2 e^{c_3 P} + c_4 e^{c_5 P} + c_6\).
GT has no pure exponential term \(e^{c_5 P}\) without \(P\) factor, and no constant. You can set \(c_4=0\) and \(c_6=0\), leaving the needed structure. Then match with \(c_0=A, c_1=B, c_2=C, c_3=-k\). **Yes.**

### 7
Contains rational terms \(\frac{P}{Pc_5+c_6}\) and \(\frac{1}{Pc_5+c_6}\). GT has none; cannot remove denominator effects unless coefficients are zero, but then those terms vanish and you’re left with \(P^2+P+P e^{cP}\) which could match. Indeed set \(c_4=0,c_7=0\) to kill rationals, and \(c_8=0\) to remove constant. Then it reduces to candidate #18 form and can match (see #18). **Yes.**

### 8
Similarly has rational-in-\(P\) terms; set their numerators to 0 to remove them and set constant to 0, leaving \(P^2+P+P e^{cP}\) structure. **Yes.**

### 9
Has \(P c_3 e^{c_4 P} + c_5 e^{c_4 P}\). GT needs only the \(P e^{cP}\) part; set \(c_5=0\) and constant \(c_6=0\). Then match with \(c_0=A\), \(c_1+c_2=B\), \(c_3=C\), \(c_4=-k\). **Yes.**

### 10
Has \(P c_0 + P^{c_1}c_2 +\) pure exponentials \(c_3 e^{c_4P}+c_5 e^{c_6P}+c_7\). There is no \(P\cdot e^{cP}\) term; exponentials are not multiplied by \(P\). Cannot represent \(P e^{-kP}\) exactly. **No.**

Constant \(c_4\) must be 0. Then it reduces to #18 with adjusted \(c_1\). **Yes.**
